<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>
<ul><li>Blue is associated with Christianity in general and Catholicism in particular, especially with the figure of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mary_(mother_of_Jesus)" title="Mary (mother of Jesus)">Virgin Mary</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></li>
<li>Blue in <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>: Many of the gods are depicted as having blue-coloured skin, particularly those associated with <a href="/wiki/Vishnu" title="Vishnu">Vishnu</a>, who is said to be the preserver of the world and thus intimately connected to water. <a href="/wiki/Krishna" title="Krishna">Krishna</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rama" title="Rama">Ram</a>, Vishnu's avatars, are usually blue. <a href="/wiki/Shiva" title="Shiva">Shiva</a>, the destroyer, is also depicted in light blue tones and is called <i>neela kantha</i>, or blue-throated, for having swallowed poison in an attempt to turn the tide of a battle between the gods and demons in the gods' favour.  Blue is used to symbolically represent the fifth, throat, <a href="/wiki/Chakra" title="Chakra">chakra</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vishuddha" title="Vishuddha">Vishuddha</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Blue_in_Judaism" title="Blue in Judaism">Blue in Judaism</a>: In the <a href="/wiki/Torah" title="Torah">Torah</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Israelites" title="Israelites">Israelites</a> were commanded to put fringes, <i><a href="/wiki/Tzitzit" title="Tzitzit">tzitzit</a></i>, on the corners of their garments, and to weave within these fringes a "twisted thread of blue (<i>tekhelet</i>)".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> In ancient days, this blue thread was made from a dye extracted from a Mediterranean snail called the <i>hilazon</i>. <a href="/wiki/Maimonides" title="Maimonides">Maimonides</a> claimed that this blue was the colour of "the clear noonday sky"; <a href="/wiki/Rashi" title="Rashi">Rashi</a>, the colour of the evening sky.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> According to several rabbinic sages, blue is the colour of God's Glory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> Staring at this colour aids in mediation, bringing us a glimpse of the "pavement of sapphire, like the very sky for purity", which is a likeness of the Throne of God.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> (The <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_language" title="Hebrew language">Hebrew</a> word for glory.) Many items in the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mishkan" title="Mishkan">Mishkan</a></i>, the portable sanctuary in the wilderness, such as the <i><a href="/wiki/Menorah_(Temple)" title="Menorah (Temple)">menorah</a></i>, many of the vessels, and the <a href="/wiki/Ark_of_the_Covenant" title="Ark of the Covenant">Ark of the Covenant</a>, were covered with blue cloth when transported from place to place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup></li></ul>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 202px"><div style="width: 202px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 200px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Western_Wall_-_by_Jacob_Rask.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Western_Wall_-_by_Jacob_Rask.jpg/300px-Western_Wall_-_by_Jacob_Rask.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Western_Wall_-_by_Jacob_Rask.jpg/451px-Western_Wall_-_by_Jacob_Rask.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Western_Wall_-_by_Jacob_Rask.jpg/600px-Western_Wall_-_by_Jacob_Rask.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div></div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p>Blue stripes on a traditional <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish" title="Jewish">Jewish</a> <a href="/wiki/Tallit" title="Tallit">tallit</a>. The blue stripes are also featured in the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Israel" title="Flag of Israel">flag of Israel</a>.
</p>
</div>
</div></li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 202px"><div style="width: 202px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 200px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Munneswaram_Vishnu.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1224" data-file-width="1632" decoding="async" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Munneswaram_Vishnu.jpg/300px-Munneswaram_Vishnu.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Munneswaram_Vishnu.jpg/451px-Munneswaram_Vishnu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Munneswaram_Vishnu.jpg/600px-Munneswaram_Vishnu.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div></div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/Vishnu" title="Vishnu">Vishnu</a>, the supreme god of <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>, is often portrayed as being blue, or more precisely having skin the colour of rain-filled clouds.
</p>
</div>
</div></li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 94.666666666667px"><div style="width: 94.666666666667px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 92.666666666667px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gentile_da_Fabriano,_Kreuzigung.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2183" data-file-width="1352" decoding="async" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Gentile_da_Fabriano%2C_Kreuzigung.jpg/139px-Gentile_da_Fabriano%2C_Kreuzigung.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Gentile_da_Fabriano%2C_Kreuzigung.jpg/209px-Gentile_da_Fabriano%2C_Kreuzigung.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Gentile_da_Fabriano%2C_Kreuzigung.jpg/279px-Gentile_da_Fabriano%2C_Kreuzigung.jpg 2x" width="93"/></a></div></div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p>In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholicism" title="Catholicism">Catholicism</a>, blue became the traditional colour of the robes of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virgin_Mary" title="Virgin Mary">Virgin Mary</a> in the 13th century.
</p>
</div>
</div></li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 104.66666666667px"><div style="width: 104.66666666667px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 102.66666666667px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MedecineBuddha.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="874" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/MedecineBuddha.JPG/154px-MedecineBuddha.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/MedecineBuddha.JPG/232px-MedecineBuddha.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/MedecineBuddha.JPG/309px-MedecineBuddha.JPG 2x" width="103"/></a></div></div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Bhaisajyaguru" title="Bhaisajyaguru">Bhaisajyaguru</a>, or "Medicine Master of Lapis Lazuli Light", is the Buddha of healing and medicine in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mahayana_Buddhism" title="Mahayana Buddhism">Mahayana Buddhism</a>. He traditionally holds a lapis lazuli jar of medicine.
</p>
</div>
</div></li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 105.33333333333px"><div style="width: 105.33333333333px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 103.33333333333px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Iranian_Tiles_1.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="3648" data-file-width="2511" decoding="async" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Iranian_Tiles_1.JPG/155px-Iranian_Tiles_1.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Iranian_Tiles_1.JPG/232px-Iranian_Tiles_1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Iranian_Tiles_1.JPG/310px-Iranian_Tiles_1.JPG 2x" width="104"/></a></div></div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p>In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islamic" title="Islamic">Islamic</a> World, blue and turquoise <a href="/wiki/Tile" title="Tile">tile</a> traditionally decorates the facades and exteriors of mosques and other religious buildings. This mosque is in <a href="/wiki/Isfahan" title="Isfahan">Isfahan</a>, Iran.
</p>
</div>
</div></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gender">Gender</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_historical_sources_for_pink_and_blue_as_gender_signifiers" title="List of historical sources for pink and blue as gender signifiers">List of historical sources for pink and blue as gender signifiers</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ANAB767300Restroomsign.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="2448" decoding="async" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/ANAB767300Restroomsign.jpg/220px-ANAB767300Restroomsign.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/ANAB767300Restroomsign.jpg/330px-ANAB767300Restroomsign.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/ANAB767300Restroomsign.jpg/440px-ANAB767300Restroomsign.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ANAB767300Restroomsign.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>This restroom sign on an <a href="/wiki/All_Nippon_Airways" title="All Nippon Airways">All Nippon Airways</a> Boeing 767-300 uses blue for the male gender</div></div></div>
<p>Blue was first used as a <a href="/wiki/Gender" title="Gender">gender</a> signifier just prior to <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> (for either girls or boys), and first established as a male gender signifier in the 1940s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span></h3>
<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/Blues" title="Blues">blues</a> is a popular musical form created in the United States in the 19th century by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African-American" title="African-American">African-American</a> musicians, based on African musical roots.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> It usually expresses sadness and melancholy.</li>
<li>A <a href="/wiki/Blue_note" title="Blue note">blue note</a> is a musical note sung or played at a slightly lower <a href="/wiki/Pitch_(music)" title="Pitch (music)">pitch</a> than the <a href="/wiki/Major_scale" title="Major scale">major scale</a> for expressive purposes, giving it a slightly melancholy sound. It is frequently used in <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">jazz</a> and the blues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bluegrass_music" title="Bluegrass music">Bluegrass</a> is a subgenre of American <a href="/wiki/Country_music" title="Country music">country music</a>, born in <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">Kentucky</a> and the mountains of <a href="/wiki/Appalachia" title="Appalachia">Appalachia</a>. It has its roots in the traditional folk music of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Folk_music_of_Scotland" title="Folk music of Scotland">Scottish</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Folk_music_of_Ireland" title="Folk music of Ireland">Irish</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span></h3>
<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Blue&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">March 2016</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<ul><li>In many countries, blue is often used as a colour for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guide_sign" title="Guide sign">guide signs</a> on highways.  In the <a href="/wiki/Manual_on_Uniform_Traffic_Control_Devices" title="Manual on Uniform Traffic Control Devices">Manual on Uniform Traffic Control Devices</a> used in the United States, as well as in other countries with MUTCD-inspired signage, blue is often used to indicate motorist services.</li>
<li>Many bus and rail systems around the world that colour code rail lines typically include a <a class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Blue_Line_(disambiguation)" title="Blue Line (disambiguation)">Blue Line</a>.</li>
<li>The colour blue has also been used extensively by several airlines.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta Air Lines</a> has used the colour blue extensively for advertising and on its aircraft for many years.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/JetBlue" title="JetBlue">JetBlue</a> is an American low-cost airline.</li></ul></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Associations_and_sayings">Associations and sayings</span></h3>
<ul><li><i>True blue</i> is an expression in the United States which means faithful and loyal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></li>
<li>In Britain, a bride in a wedding is encouraged to wear "<a href="/wiki/Something_old" title="Something old">Something old, something new, something borrowed, something blue</a>," as a sign of loyalty and faithfulness.  A blue sapphire engagement ring is also considered a symbol of fidelity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup></li>
<li>Blue is often associated with excellence, distinction and high performance. The Queen of the United Kingdom and the Chancellor of Germany often wear a blue sash at formal occasions. In the United States, the <a href="/wiki/Blue_ribbon" title="Blue ribbon">blue ribbon</a> is usually the highest award in expositions and county fairs. The <a href="/wiki/Blue_Riband" title="Blue Riband">Blue Riband</a> was a trophy and flag given to the fastest transatlantic steamships in the 19th and 20th century. A <a href="/wiki/Blue-ribbon_panel" title="Blue-ribbon panel">blue-ribbon panel</a> is a group of top-level experts selected to examine a subject.</li>
<li>A <a href="/wiki/Blue_chip_(stock_market)" title="Blue chip (stock market)">blue chip</a> stock is a stock in a company with a reputation for quality and reliability in good times and bad. The term was invented in the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange" title="New York Stock Exchange">New York Stock Exchange</a> in 1923 or 1924, and comes from <a href="/wiki/Poker" title="Poker">poker</a>, where the highest value chips are blue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></li>
<li>Someone with blue blood is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Nobility" title="Nobility">nobility</a>. The term comes from the Spanish <i>sangre azul</i>, and is said to refer to the pale skin and prominent blue veins of Spanish nobles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated5_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated5-123">[123]</a></sup></li>
<li>Blue is also associated with labour and the working class. It is the common colour of overalls <a href="/wiki/Jeans" title="Jeans">blue jeans</a> and other working costumes. In the United States "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blue_collar" title="Blue collar">blue collar</a>" workers refers to those who, in either skilled or unskilled jobs, work with their hands and do not wear business suits ("white collar" workers).</li>
<li>Blue is traditionally associated with the sea and the sky, with infinity and distance. The uniforms of sailors are usually dark blue, those of air forces lighter blue. The expression <i> "The wild blue yonder" </i> in the <a href="/wiki/The_U.S._Air_Force_(song)" title="The U.S. Air Force (song)"> official song of the U.S. Air Force</a> refers to the sky.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup></li>
<li>Blue is associated with cold water taps which are traditionally marked with blue.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bluestocking" title="Bluestocking">Bluestocking</a> was an unflattering expression in the 18th century for upper-class women who cared about culture and intellectual life and disregarded fashion. It originally referred to men and women who wore plain blue wool stockings instead of the black silk stockings worn in society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated5_123-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated5-123">[123]</a></sup></li>
<li>Blue is often associated with <a href="/wiki/Depression_(mood)" title="Depression (mood)">melancholy</a> – having the "blues".</li>
<li>In English-speaking countries, the colour blue is sometimes associated with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sexually_suggestive" title="Sexually suggestive">risqué</a>, for example "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blue_comedy" title="Blue comedy">blue comedy</a>", "<a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/blue_movie" title="wikt:blue movie">blue movie</a>" (a euphemism for a <a href="/wiki/Pornographic_film" title="Pornographic film">pornographic film</a>) or "turning the air blue" (an idiom referring to profuse swearing).</li>
<li>The colour blue is typically associated with <a href="/wiki/Autism" title="Autism">autism</a> and the charity <a href="/wiki/Autism_Speaks" title="Autism Speaks">Autism Speaks</a>. However, due to controversy surrounding attitudes which the organization promotes pertaining to the disorder, a new, much smaller movement exists to associate autism with the colour red.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li></ul>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:15px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Charles_Andr%C3%A9_Van_Loo_-_Madame_de_Pompadour_en_belle_jardini%C3%A8re_-_v.1754-1755.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2102" data-file-width="1675" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Charles_Andr%C3%A9_Van_Loo_-_Madame_de_Pompadour_en_belle_jardini%C3%A8re_-_v.1754-1755.jpg/96px-Charles_Andr%C3%A9_Van_Loo_-_Madame_de_Pompadour_en_belle_jardini%C3%A8re_-_v.1754-1755.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Charles_Andr%C3%A9_Van_Loo_-_Madame_de_Pompadour_en_belle_jardini%C3%A8re_-_v.1754-1755.jpg/143px-Charles_Andr%C3%A9_Van_Loo_-_Madame_de_Pompadour_en_belle_jardini%C3%A8re_-_v.1754-1755.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Charles_Andr%C3%A9_Van_Loo_-_Madame_de_Pompadour_en_belle_jardini%C3%A8re_-_v.1754-1755.jpg/191px-Charles_Andr%C3%A9_Van_Loo_-_Madame_de_Pompadour_en_belle_jardini%C3%A8re_-_v.1754-1755.jpg 2x" width="96"/></a></div></div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Madame_Pompadour" title="Madame Pompadour">Madame Pompadour</a>, the mistress of King <a href="/wiki/Louis_XV_of_France" title="Louis XV of France">Louis XV of France</a>, wore blue <a href="/wiki/Myosotis" title="Myosotis">myosotis</a>, or forget-me-not flowers in her hair and on her gowns as a symbol of faithfulness to the king.
</p>
</div>
</div></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rink_bandy_ball.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Rink_bandy_ball.JPG/220px-Rink_bandy_ball.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Rink_bandy_ball.JPG/330px-Rink_bandy_ball.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Rink_bandy_ball.JPG/440px-Rink_bandy_ball.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rink_bandy_ball.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rinkball" title="Rinkball">rinkball</a> a blue <a href="/wiki/Ball" title="Ball">ball</a> is used</div></div></div>
<p>Many sporting teams make blue their official colour, or use it as detail on kit of a different colour. In addition, the colour is present on the logos of many sports associations. Along with <a href="/wiki/Red" title="Red">red</a>, blue is the most commonly used non-white colours for teams.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_blues_of_antiquity">The blues of antiquity</span></h3>
<ul><li>In the late <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a>, during the time of <a href="/wiki/Caligula" title="Caligula">Caligula</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nero" title="Nero">Nero</a> and the emperors who followed, the Blues were a popular chariot racing team which competed in the <a href="/wiki/Circus_Maximus" title="Circus Maximus">Circus Maximus</a> in Rome against the Greens, the Reds and Whites.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Edward_Gibbon_1960_pg._554_102-1"><a href="#cite_note-Edward_Gibbon_1960_pg._554-102">[102]</a></sup></li>
<li>In the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a>, The Blues and Greens were the two most popular chariot racing teams which competed in the <a href="/wiki/Hippodrome_of_Constantinople" title="Hippodrome of Constantinople">Hippodrome of Constantinople</a>. Each was connected with a powerful political faction, and disputes between the Green and Blue supporters often became violent. After one competition in 532 AD, during the reign of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emperor_Justinian" title="Emperor Justinian">Emperor Justinian</a>, riots between the two factions broke out, during which the cathedral and much of the centre of Constantinople were burned, and more than thirty thousand people were killed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> (See <a href="/wiki/Nika_riots" title="Nika riots">Nika riots</a>)</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Association_football">Association football</span></h3>
<p>In international <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">association football</a>, blue is a common colour on kits, as a majority of nations wear the colours of their national flag. A notable exception is four-time <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a> winners <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_football_team" title="Italy national football team">Italy</a>, who wear a blue kit based on the <i>Azzuro Savoia</i> (<a href="/wiki/Savoy" title="Savoy">Savoy</a> blue) of the royal <a href="/wiki/House_of_Savoy" title="House of Savoy">House of Savoy</a> which unified the Italian states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> The team themselves are known as <i>Gli Azzurri</i> (the Blues). Another World Cup winning nation with a blue shirt is <a href="/wiki/France_national_football_team" title="France national football team">France</a>, who are known as <i>Les Bleus</i> (the Blues). Two neighbouring countries with two World Cup victories each, <a href="/wiki/Argentina_national_football_team" title="Argentina national football team">Argentina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uruguay_national_football_team" title="Uruguay national football team">Uruguay</a> wear a light blue shirt, the former with white stripes. Uruguay are known as the <i>La Celeste</i>, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> for 'the <a href="/wiki/Sky_blue" title="Sky blue">sky blue</a> one', while Argentina are known as <i>Los Albicelestes</i>, Spanish for 'the sky blue and whites'.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup>
</p><p>Blue features on the logo of football's governing body <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a>, as well as featuring highly in the design of their website.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> The European governing body of football, <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a>, uses two tones of blue to create a map of Europe in the centre of their logo. The <a href="/wiki/Asian_Football_Confederation" title="Asian Football Confederation">Asian Football Confederation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oceania_Football_Confederation" title="Oceania Football Confederation">Oceania Football Confederation</a> and <a href="/wiki/CONCACAF" title="CONCACAF">CONCACAF</a> (the governing body of football in North and Central America and the Caribbean) use blue text on their logos.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="North_American_sporting_leagues">North American sporting leagues</span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a>, the premier baseball league in the United States and Canada, blue is one of the three colours, along with white and red, on the league's official logo. A team from <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a> are nicknamed the <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Blue_Jays" title="Toronto Blue Jays">Blue Jays</a>. Seventeen other teams either regularly feature blue hats or utilise the colour in their uniforms.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">National Basketball Association</a>, the premier <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a> league in the United States and Canada, also has blue as one of the colours on their logo, along with red and white also, as did its female equivalent, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WNBA" title="WNBA">WNBA</a>, until March 28, 2011, when the latter adopted an orange and white logo. Former NBA player <a href="/wiki/Blue_Edwards" title="Blue Edwards">Theodore Edwards</a> was nicknamed "Blue". Fifteen NBA teams feature the colour in their uniforms.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">National Football League</a>, the premier <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">American football</a> league in the United States, also uses blue as one of three colours, along with white and red, on their official logo. Thirteen NFL teams prominently feature the colour .
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">National Hockey League</a>, the premier <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">Ice hockey</a> league in Canada and the United States, uses blue on its official logo. Blue is the main colour of many teams in the league: the <a href="/wiki/Buffalo_Sabres" title="Buffalo Sabres">Buffalo Sabres</a>, <a href="/wiki/Columbus_Blue_Jackets" title="Columbus Blue Jackets">Columbus Blue Jackets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edmonton_Oilers" title="Edmonton Oilers">Edmonton Oilers</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_Islanders" title="New York Islanders">New York Islanders</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_Rangers" title="New York Rangers">New York Rangers</a>, <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Blues" title="St. Louis Blues">St. Louis Blues</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Maple_Leafs" title="Toronto Maple Leafs">Toronto Maple Leafs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tampa_Bay_Lightning" title="Tampa Bay Lightning">Tampa Bay Lightning</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vancouver_Canucks" title="Vancouver Canucks">Vancouver Canucks</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_Jets" title="Winnipeg Jets">Winnipeg Jets</a>.
</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:37.5px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Italia_v_Francia_Mondiale_1978.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="377" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="75" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/be/Italia_v_Francia_Mondiale_1978.jpg/120px-Italia_v_Francia_Mondiale_1978.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/be/Italia_v_Francia_Mondiale_1978.jpg/180px-Italia_v_Francia_Mondiale_1978.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/be/Italia_v_Francia_Mondiale_1978.jpg/240px-Italia_v_Francia_Mondiale_1978.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a></div></div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_football_team" title="Italy national football team">Italian national football team</a> wear blue in honour of the royal <a href="/wiki/House_of_Savoy" title="House of Savoy">House of Savoy</a> which unified the country.
</p>
</div>
</div></li>
</ul>
